<details>

**Input:**

*Get full body of all 6 issues*

```bash
for i in 207 208 209 210 211 212; do echo "=== Issue #$i ===" && gh issue view $i --json title,body --jq '"\(.title)\n\(.body)"' 2>&1 && echo ""; done
```

**Result:**

Loading .zprofile at 19:42:41
=== Issue #207 ===
AMP messages missing fromLabel/toLabel in convertAMPToMessage
In `lib/messageQueue.ts`, the `convertAMPToMessage()` function (around line 215-233) never populates `fromLabel` or `toLabel` fields on the returned Message object. The Message interface defines these fields (lines 27, 33), and the old flat-format MessageSummary populates them (lines 318-319), but AMP-format messages always have undefined labels.

This means AMP messages display without sender/recipient labels in the UI.

Found during AIM-222 audit.

=== Issue #208 ===
AMP signature verification data lost during message format conversion
In `lib/messageQueue.ts`, the `convertAMPToMessage()` function never populates the `amp` field (interface lines 60-67) which holds cryptographic verification data (`signature`, `senderPublicKey`, `signatureVerified`, etc.). The raw AMP envelope likely contains this data but it's discarded during conversion.

This means signature verification status is lost when displaying AMP messages.

Found during AIM-222 audit.

=== Issue #209 ===
GET /api/agents/[id] returns 404 for soft-deleted agents (no includeDeleted support)
In `app/api/agents/[id]/route.ts`, the GET handler calls `getAgent(params.id)` without `includeDeleted=true`. This means soft-deleted agents return 404, with no way to inspect a soft-deleted agent's details before hard-deleting or restoring it.

Suggestion: Add `?includeDeleted=true` query parameter support to the GET handler.

Found during AIM-222 audit.

=== Issue #210 ===
chat/route.ts GET handler uses inconsistent target quoting in capture-pane
In `app/api/agents/[id]/chat/route.ts`, the GET handler's tmux capture-pane command (around line 174) uses single-quoted session target while the POST handler (fixed in PR #206) and all other tmux files use double-quoted targets.

This is a cosmetic inconsistency — both work — but should be normalized for maintainability.

Found during AIM-222 audit.

=== Issue #211

   193→  const envelope = ampMsg.envelope
   194→  const payload = ampMsg.payload

   192→function convertAMPToMessage(ampMsg: any): Message | null {
   193→  const envelope = ampMsg.envelope
   194→  const payload = ampMsg.payload
   195→  if (!envelope || !payload) return null
   196→
   197→  const fromName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.from)
   198→  const toName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.to)
   199→  const fromHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.from)
   200→  const toHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.to)
   201→  const id = normalizeMessageId(envelope.id)
   202→  const status = ampMsg.metadata?.status || ampMsg.local?.status || 'unread'
   203→
   204→  return {
   205→    id,
   206→    from: fromName,
   207→    fromAlias: fromName,
   208→    fromHost,
   209→    to: toName,
   210→    toAlias: toName,
   211→    toHost,
   212→    timestamp: envelope.timestamp,
   213→    subject: envelope.subject,
   214→    priority: envelope.priority || 'normal',
   215→    status: status as Message['status'],
   216→    content: {
   217→      type: payload.type || 'notification',
   218→      message: payload.message || '',
   219→      context: payload.context || undefined,
   220→    },
   221→    inReplyTo: envelope.in_reply_to || undefined,
   222→  }
   223→}

**New:**
```
  const fromName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.from)
  const toName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.to)
  const fromHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.from)
  const toHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.to)
  const id = normalizeMessageId(envelope.id)
  const status = ampMsg.metadata?.status || ampMsg.local?.status || 'unread'

  // Resolve display labels from agent registry (falls back to name if no label set)
  const fromAgent = getAgentByName(fromName) || getAgentByAlias(fromName)
  const toAgent = getAgentByName(toName) || getAgentByAlias(toName)
  const fromLabel = fromAgent?.label || fromName
  const toLabel = toAgent?.label || toName

  return {
    id,
    from: fromName,
    fromAlias: fromName,
    fromLabel,
    fromHost,
    to: toName,
    toAlias: toName,
    toLabel,
    toHost,
```

**Input:**

*Commit fix for issue 207*

```bash
git add lib/messageQueue.ts && git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
fix(amp): populate fromLabel/toLabel in convertAMPToMessage (#207)

AMP-format messages were missing display labels because
convertAMPToMessage() never resolved agent labels from the registry.
Old flat-format messages had labels stored in the JSON, but AMP
envelopes only carry addresses, not display names.

Look up sender/receiver agents via getAgentByName/getAgentByAlias
and populate fromLabel/toLabel, falling back to the raw name.

Closes #207
EOF
)"
```

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:46:42]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Create PR for issue 207</summary>

**Input:**

*Create PR for issue 207*

```bash
gh pr create --repo 23blocks-OS/ai-maestro --head Emasoft:fix/issue-207-amp-labels --base main --title "fix(amp): populate fromLabel/toLabel in convertAMPToMessage" --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Summary

- AMP-format messages were missing display labels (`fromLabel`/`toLabel`) because `convertAMPToMessage()` never resolved agent labels from the registry
- Old flat-format messages had labels stored in the JSON file, but AMP envelopes only carry addresses
- Now resolves sender/receiver agents via `getAgentByName`/`getAgentByAlias` and populates labels, falling back to the raw name

## Test Plan

- [ ] Send AMP message between agents with labels set
- [ ] Verify UI shows display labels instead of raw session names
- [ ] Verify agents without labels fall back to name correctly

Closes #207
EOF
)" 2>&1
```

   307→export async function writeToAMPInbox(
   308→  envelope: AMPEnvelope,
   309→  payload: AMPPayload,
   310→  recipientAgent?: string,
   311→  senderPublicKey?: string,
   312→  recipientAgentId?: string
   313→): Promise<string | null> {
   314→  try {
   315→    const agentName = recipientAgent || extractAgentName(envelope.to)
   316→    if (!agentName) {
   317→      console.error('[AMP Inbox Writer] Cannot determine recipient agent name')
   318→      return null
   319→    }
   320→
   321→    const agentHome = resolveAgentAMPHome(agentName, recipientAgentId)
   322→    const agentInboxDir = path.join(agentHome, 'messages', 'inbox')
   323→    const senderDir = sanitizeAddressForPath(envelope.from)
   324→    const inboxSenderDir = path.join(agentInboxDir, senderDir)
   325→
   326→    await fs.mkdir(inboxSenderDir, { recursive: true })
   327→
   328→    const ampMessage = {
   329→      envelope: {
   330→        version: envelope.version || 'amp/0.1',
   331→        id: envelope.id,
   332→        from: envelope.from,
   333→        to: envelope.to,

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:47:39]*

Now I can see the structure. The stored JSON has `envelope.signature` and `sender_public_key` at the top level. When `convertAMPToMessage` reads this, it should map these to the `amp` field. Let me apply the fix.


## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:47:45]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `messageQueue.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/messageQueue.ts`

**Old:**
```
  return {
    id,
    from: fromName,
    fromAlias: fromName,
    fromHost,
    to: toName,
    toAlias: toName,
    toHost,
    timestamp: envelope.timestamp,
    subject: envelope.subject,
    priority: envelope.priority || 'normal',
    status: status as Message['status'],
    content: {
      type: payload.type || 'notification',
      message: payload.message || '',
      context: payload.context || undefined,
    },
    inReplyTo: envelope.in_reply_to || undefined,
  }
```

**New:**
```
  // Preserve AMP cryptographic verification data from the stored message
  const senderPublicKey = ampMsg.sender_public_key as string | undefined
  const amp: Message['amp'] = (envelope.signature || senderPublicKey) ? {
    signature: envelope.signature || undefined,
    senderPublicKey: senderPublicKey || undefined,
    // signatureVerified is not stored on disk — would need runtime verification
    ampAddress: envelope.from || undefined,
    envelopeId: envelope.id || undefined,
  } : undefined

  return {
    id,
    from: fromName,
    fromAlias: fromName,
    fromHost,
    to: toName,
    toAlias: toName,
    toHost,
    timestamp: envelope.timestamp,
    subject: envelope.subject,
    priority: envelope.priority || 'normal',
    status: status as Message['status'],
    content: {
      type: payload.type || 'notification',
      message: payload.message || '',
      context: payload.context || undefined,
    },
    inReplyTo: envelope.in_reply_to || undefined,
    amp,
  }
```

**Result:**

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:48:16]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Commit and push fix for issue 208</summary>

**Input:**

*Commit and push fix for issue 208*

```bash
git add lib/messageQueue.ts && git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
fix(amp): preserve signature verification data in convertAMPToMessage (#208)

The convertAMPToMessage() function discarded cryptographic verification
data (signature, senderPublicKey) stored in AMP inbox files. The raw
envelope contains signature and the top-level sender_public_key field,
but these were never mapped to the Message.amp interface fields.

Now extracts envelope.signature and sender_public_key from stored
AMP messages and populates the amp field with signature, senderPublicKey,
ampAddress, and envelopeId.

Closes #208
EOF
)" && git push fork fix/issue-208-amp-signature 2>&1
```

     5→/**

     7→ * Get a specific agent by ID
     8→ */
     9→export async function GET(
    10→  request: Request,
    11→  { params }: { params: { id: string } }
    12→) {
    13→  try {
    14→    const agent = getAgent(params.id)
    15→
    16→    if (!agent) {
    17→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Agent not found' }, { status: 404 })
    18→    }
    19→
    20→    return NextResponse.json({ agent })
    21→  } catch (error) {
    22→    console.error('Failed to get agent:', error)
    23→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Failed to get agent' }, { status: 500 })
    24→  }
    25→}

    28→ * PATCH /api/agents/[id]

    31→export async function PATCH(
    32→  request: Request,
    33→  { params }: { params: { id: string } }
    34→) {

    36→    const body: UpdateAgentRequest = await request.json()
    37→

    47→    console.error('Failed to update agent:', error)
    48→    return NextResponse.json({ error: message }, { status: 400 })
    49→  }
    50→}

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:49:04]*

Interesting — on `main`, there's no `deletedAt` field at all. That was introduced in PR #206. So issue #209 about soft-deleted agents is actually a feature that depends on PR #206 landing first. Let me check the issue again.

The issue says: *"GET /api/agents/[id] returns 404 for soft-deleted agents (no includeDeleted support)"* — but since `deletedAt` doesn't exist on `main`, this issue only makes sense after PR #206 is merged. This is actually a follow-up feature request, not a standalone bug on `main`.

Let me check if the other issues (#210, #211, #212) exist on `main`.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:51:07]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Bash -- Commit and push fix for issue 210</summary>

**Input:**

*Commit and push fix for issue 210*

```bash
git add "app/api/agents/[id]/chat/route.ts" && git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
fix(chat): normalize tmux target quoting to double quotes (#210)

The chat route used single-quoted tmux targets (-t '${sessionName}')
while all other tmux commands in the codebase use double quotes
(-t "${sessionName}"). Normalized to double quotes for consistency.

Single quotes work identically for alphanumeric session names, but
double quotes are the established convention throughout the project.

Closes #210
EOF
)" && git push fork fix/issue-210-chat-quoting 2>&1
```

**Result:**

*Commit and push fix for issue 211*

```bash
git add install.sh && git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
fix(install): quote variables to prevent word-splitting (#211)

Line 284: $NODE_VERSION was unquoted in echo pipe — could
word-split if version string ever contained spaces.

Line 982: $INSTALL_DIR was unquoted in display echo — shows
users a cd command that would fail on paths with spaces.

Closes #211
EOF
)" && git push fork fix/issue-211-install-unquoted 2>&1
```

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:52:47]*

The script doesn't parse arguments at all, so passing `-y` won't cause an error (bash ignores unused positional params). The fix is straightforward: add `-y` to the invocation for consistency.

   701→  const agents = loadAgents()
   702→  const agentToDelete = agents.find(a => a.id === id)
   703→
   704→  if (!agentToDelete) {
   705→    return false // Agent not found
   706→  }

   712→

   714→    // --- Soft-delete path: mark as deleted, preserve all data on disk ---
   715→    const agentIndex = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === id)
   716→    agents[agentIndex].deletedAt = new Date().toISOString()
   717→    agents[agentIndex].status = 'deleted'
   718→    saveAgents(agents)

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:54:26]*

The default `deleteAgent(id)` (no `hard` param) does a soft-delete — marks the agent with `deletedAt` and `status: 'deleted'` but keeps it in the array. The tests expect the agent to be removed from `loadAgents()`, but now it's still there, just soft-deleted.

I need to update the tests. The test "removes agent from registry" should verify soft-delete behavior (agent still in array but marked deleted), and add a separate test for hard delete.


## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 19:54:36]*

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/tests/agent-registry.test.ts`

**Old:**
```
describe('deleteAgent', () => {
  it('removes agent from registry', () => {
    const agent = createAgent(makeCreateRequest({ name: 'delete-me' }))
    expect(loadAgents()).toHaveLength(1)

    const result = deleteAgent(agent.id)
    expect(result).toBe(true)
    expect(loadAgents()).toHaveLength(0)
  })

  it('returns false for non-existent agent', () => {
    const result = deleteAgent('nonexistent-id')
    expect(result).toBe(false)
  })

  it('removes the correct agent when multiple exist', () => {
    const a1 = createAgent(makeCreateRequest({ name: 'keep-me' }))
    const a2 = createAgent(makeCreateRequest({ name: 'delete-me' }))

    deleteAgent(a2.id)
    const remaining = loadAgents()
    expect(remaining).toHaveLength(1)
    expect(remaining[0].id).toBe(a1.id)
  })
})
```

**New:**
```
describe('deleteAgent', () => {
  it('soft-deletes agent by default (marks deletedAt, keeps in registry)', () => {
    const agent = createAgent(makeCreateRequest({ name: 'delete-me' }))
    expect(loadAgents()).toHaveLength(1)

    const result = deleteAgent(agent.id)
    expect(result).toBe(true)
    // Soft-delete keeps agent in array but marks it deleted
    const agents = loadAgents()
    expect(agents).toHaveLength(1)
    expect(agents[0].deletedAt).toBeDefined()
    expect(agents[0].status).toBe('deleted')
  })

  it('hard-deletes agent when hard=true (removes from registry)', () => {
    const agent = createAgent(makeCreateRequest({ name: 'hard-delete-me' }))
    expect(loadAgents()).toHaveLength(1)

    const result = deleteAgent(agent.id, true)
    expect(result).toBe(true)
    expect(loadAgents()).toHaveLength(0)
  })

  it('returns false for non-existent agent', () => {
    const result = deleteAgent('nonexistent-id')
    expect(result).toBe(false)
  })

    const a1 = createAgent(makeCreateRequest({ name: 'k

<summary>Agent "Fix install-messaging.sh backup" completed</summary>
<result>Syntax check passed (no errors). Both fixes are verified:

1. **Backup guard now blocks install**: If backup fails, `SKILL_INSTALL_OK=false` prevents the `cp -r` from running, so the existing skill is never overwritten without a backup.

2. **Copy-then-swap pattern**: New version is copied to a temp directory first (`mktemp -d`). Only after the copy succeeds does `rm -rf` + `mv` happen. If the copy fails, the temp dir is cleaned up and the backup is restored if the original was somehow lost.

[DONE] fix-pr206-install-messaging - Fixed both backup-guard-defeated-by-unconditional-cp and rm-before-cp-could-fail patterns in `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/install-messaging.sh` (lines 714-791).
